Section 1:
A.B. 5
ON JOBS AND ECONOMY
PREFILED NOVEMBER 12, 2025
____________
Referred to Select Committee on Jobs and Economy
SUMMARY—Enacts the Nevada Studio Infrastructure Jobs and
Workforce Training Act. (BDR S-13)
FISCAL NOTE: Effect on Local Government: May have Fiscal Impact.
Effect on the State: Yes.
~
EXPLANATION – Matter in bolded italics is new; matter between brackets [omitted material] is material to be omitted.
AN ACT relating to economic development; enacting the Nevada
Studio Infrastructure Jobs and Workforce Training Act;
requiring the Office of Economic Development to enter
into a development agreement to establish certain criteria
for the development of infrastructure for the production of
motion pictures and other qualified productions and other
new capital investment in this State; establishing certain
penalties if the development does not meet certain
requirements for new capital investment and expenditures
for the production of motion pictures and other qualified
productions; establishing requirements for a production
company located at such a development to be eligible for
film infrastructure transferable tax credits for qualified
productions produced at the development; providing for
the calculation of the amount of film infrastructure
transferable tax credits; requiring the creation of a
production studio entertainment district; revising
provisions governing noninfrastructure transferable tax
credits for motion pictures and other qualified productions
produced in this State; authorizing an additional amount
of noninfrastructure transferable tax credits; establishing
the Account for Nevada Film, Media and Related
Technology Education and Vocational Training and a
board to approve distributions from the Account;
providing for the distribution of money from the Account
-
*AB5*
– 2 –
to certain entities and organizations that provide
education and vocational training to develop a workforce
for the production of qualified productions in this State;
and providing other matters properly relating thereto.
Legislative Counsel’s Digest:
1 Existing law establishes a program for the issuance of transferable tax credits
2 by the Office of Economic Development to the production company of a motion
3 picture or other qualified production, based upon qualified direct production
4 expenditures made for the purchase of personal property or services from a Nevada
5 business. (NRS 360.758-360.7598) This bill revises provisions governing these
6 transferable tax credits and enacts the Nevada Studio Infrastructure Jobs and
7 Workforce Training Act to authorize film infrastructure transferable tax credits for
8 qualified productions produced at the site of the Summerlin Production Studios
9 Project.
10 Sections 1-20 of this bill enact the Nevada Studio Infrastructure Jobs and
11 Workforce Training Act, which provides film infrastructure transferable tax credits
12 for production companies located within the Summerlin Production Studios Project,
13 as defined in section 9. Section 10 requires the Office of Economic Development
14 to enter into a development agreement with the lead participant of the Project to
15 establish: (1) certain criteria that the Project is required to satisfy for film
16 infrastructure transferable tax credits to be authorized for qualified productions at
17 the Project; and (2) certain requirements for new capital investment in this State
18 and the generation of direct production expenditures in this State, which the Project
19 must meet, with certain exceptions, to avoid penalties specified in section 10.
20 Section 11: (1) authorizes production companies located at the Project to apply, on
21 or after December 1, 2026, to the Office for film infrastructure transferable tax
22 credits for qualified productions produced, in whole or in part, at the Project; and
23 (2) authorizes such credits to be used against the modified business tax, insurance
24 premium tax or gaming license fee, or any combination of these taxes and fees.
25 Section 12 establishes the qualified direct production expenditures which are the
26 basis for calculating the amount of film infrastructure transferable tax credits,
27 including, without limitation: (1) purchases, rentals or leases of property or services
28 from a Nevada business; (2) wages and fringe benefits paid to employees who are
29 Nevada residents or other personnel for labor or services provided in this State on
30 the qualified production; and (3) amounts paid to service providers for the services
31 of certain persons on the qualified production. Section 13 establishes requirements
32 for the employment of Nevada residents as below-the-line employees of qualified
33 productions. Section 14 provides that the base amount of film infrastructure
34 transferable tax credits is 30 percent of the amount of qualified direct production
35 expenditures calculated under section 12, with certain reductions if the production
36 company does not satisfy certain criteria for work opportunities to members of
37 traditionally underrepresented groups. Section 15: (1) limits the total amount of
38 film infrastructure transferable tax credits issued pursuant to sections 1-20 to
39 $95,000,000 for each fiscal year beginning on or after July 1, 2029; and (2)
40 prohibits the approval of an application for film infrastructure transferable tax
41 credits if the application is submitted in a fiscal year that begins on or after July 1,
42 2044. Section 16 requires a production company to: (1) commence principal
43 photography within a certain period of time after the Office approves an application
44 for a certificate of eligibility for film infrastructure transferable tax credits; (2)
45 complete the qualified production within 18 months after the date of
46 commencement of principal photography, except that the Office may extend this
47 period for not more than 6 months; and (3) submit certain required information
48 within the required period. Section 17 requires a production company to repay film
-
*AB5*
– 3 –
49 infrastructure transferable tax credits under certain circumstances. Section 19
50 requires the lead participant in the Project to submit certain reports to the Governor,
51 the Legislature and the Office. Section 20 requires certain reports to be made to the
52 Legislature concerning film infrastructure transferable tax credits.
53 Sections 23-32 of this bill make various changes to the existing law governing
54 the noninfrastructure transferable tax credits for motion picture and other qualified
55 productions. (NRS 360.758-360.7598) Section 24 changes references to “extras” in
56 a qualification production to “background actors.” Section 25: (1) provides that
57 digital media productions are qualified productions for the purposes of eligibility
58 for film infrastructure transferable tax credits and noninfrastructure transferable tax
59 credits; and (2) clarifies that media productions solely produced for social media
60 are not eligible for such transferable tax credits. Section 26 revises the criteria to be
61 eligible for noninfrastructure transferable tax credits to be the same as the criteria
62 for film infrastructure transferable tax credits by: (1) removing the requirement that
63 a certain percentage of direct production expenditures be incurred in this State and,
64 instead, requiring that at least 50 percent of the total principal photography days of
65 the qualified production take place in this State or a certain amount of qualified
66 direct production expenditures be incurred in this State; and (2) requiring a
67 production company to have a workforce plan that establishes certain goals and
68 provide to the Office a final assessment of whether the production company met or
69 made a good faith effort to meet those goals. Section 22 of this bill applies to
70 applicants for noninfrastructure transferable tax credits the same requirements for
71 the employment of Nevada residents as below-the-line personnel that apply to
72 applicants for film infrastructure transferable tax credits. Section 27 revises the
73 expenditures and costs that may serve as a basis for noninfrastructure transferable
74 tax credits. Section 28: (1) increases the base amount of transferable tax credits
75 from 15 percent of the qualified direct production expenditures to 30 percent of the
76 qualified direct production expenditures, for an application submitted in each fiscal
77 year beginning on or after July 1, 2029, and ending before July 1, 2044; and (2)
78 provides for certain reductions to that base amount during that period. Section 29
79 makes certain provisions of existing law relating to the calculation of
80 noninfrastructure transferable tax credits inapplicable for the period beginning on
81 July 1, 2029, and ending on June 30, 2044. Section 30 temporarily increases from
82 $10,000,000 to $25,000,000 the total amount of noninfrastructure transferable tax
83 credits for motion picture and other qualified productions that may be issued under
84 the existing program for each fiscal year beginning on or after July 1, 2029, until
85 June 30, 2044. Sections 31 and 32 make conforming changes so that
86 noninfrastructure transferable tax credits are administered and reported in the same
87 manner as film infrastructure transferable tax credits.
88 Section 18 requires the Clark County Board of County Commissioners to
89 create a production studio entertainment district for the purpose of enhancing early
90 childhood education opportunities, including prekindergarten, for children in Clark
91 County. Under section 18, the boundaries of the district are required to be entirely
92 within the unincorporated areas of Clark County and include only parcels of land
93 that are located within the boundaries of the Summerlin Production Studios Project.
94 Section 18 requires certain taxes on transient lodging, certain property taxes and
95 certain sales and use taxes imposed in the district to be pledged and distributed to
96 the Clark County School District and used by the Clark County School District
97 solely for the purposes of prekindergarten programs in the Clark County School
98 District. Finally, section 18 requires the Clark County School District to submit
99 annual reports to the Office concerning the use of money distributed to Clark
100 County School District under section 18.
101 Sections 33-40 of this bill establish a program to provide grants to certain
102 organizations that provide education and vocational training for workforce
103 development for the production of motion pictures and other qualified productions.
-
*AB5*
– 4 –
104 Section 38 establishes the Account for Nevada Film, Media and Related
105 Technology Education and Vocational Training for the purpose of allocating
106 money to certain entities and organizations that provide education and vocational
107 training for such workforce development. Sections 11 and 26 require a production
108 company that is issued transferable tax credits for a qualified production to pay to
109 the Office an amount of money equal to 1 percentage point of the percent of
110 qualified direct production expenditures used to calculate the amount of
111 transferable tax credits issued to the qualified production, and requires the Office to
112 deposit that money with the State Treasurer for credit to the Account. Section 39
113 creates and provides for the composition of the Board for Nevada Film, Media and
114 Related Technology Education and Vocational Training within the Office of
115 Economic Development. Section 40: (1) requires the Board to establish the
116 procedure for a person or entity to apply for a grant of money from the Account, the
117 criteria to be used to determine whether to approve an application for a grant from
118 the Account to an applicant and the requirements for reports by recipients of such
119 grants concerning the use of the grants; and (2) prohibits the making of a grant from
120 the Account unless the Board approves the application for the grant.
THE PEOPLE OF THE STATE OF NEVADA, REPRESENTED IN
SENATE AND ASSEMBLY, DO ENACT AS FOLLOWS:
1 Section 1. Sections 1 to 20, inclusive, of this act may be cited
2 as the Nevada Studio Infrastructure Jobs and Workforce Training
3 Act.
4 Sec. 2. 1. The Legislature hereby finds and declares that:
5 (a) The Las Vegas Metropolitan Area is the largest metropolitan
6 area in this State and has a site available to be developed to create
7 large-scale facilities for the location of companies that produce
8 motion pictures, television programs and other qualified productions
9 in this State. The establishment of such a studio campus will create
10 jobs in Nevada’s creative industries and diversify the economy of
11 this State.
12 (b) The Las Vegas Metropolitan Area possesses unique
13 geographic, economic and resource advantages that make it
14 especially suitable for a project of this magnitude. Because of these
15 unique local conditions, it is necessary to enact a law of local and
16 special application to promote and secure the benefits of a large-
17 scale film and media production development in Southern Nevada
18 for the benefit of the entire State.
19 (c) Because of these special characteristics and circumstances in
20 Southern Nevada, a general law cannot be made applicable to
21 achieve the purposes of this Act and a law of local and special
22 application is necessary to promote and secure the advantages of the
23 local and special characteristics and circumstances within the Las
24 Vegas Metropolitan Area.
25 2. The Legislature further finds and declares that the content
26 production industry has presented an ambitious and visionary plan
-
*AB5*
– 5 –
1 for all of Southern Nevada, which leverages the region’s unique
2 geographic assets, economic capabilities and infrastructural
3 advantages. The industry’s vision will promote the generation of
4 thousands of high-quality, high-paying jobs, billions of dollars in
5 incremental capital investments and billions more in new economic
6 output and ongoing spending. This plan transcends the development
7 of a mere studio complex, proposing instead a dynamic production
8 campus that is intended to serve as the nucleus for a robust,
9 sustainable industrial cluster. The Legislature recognizes that
10 realizing this vision depends fundamentally upon a collaborative
11 public-private partnership, wherein the State’s commitment,
12 provided through transferable tax credits, creates leverage that
13 significantly multiplies the benefits accruing to this State. In
14 entering this partnership, the Legislature affirms its clear and
15 unwavering expectation that if the industry benefits from the State’s
16 contribution of transferable tax credits, the industry’s promises will
17 be fulfilled, the outcomes articulated by the industry will be met or
18 exceeded, and the anticipated economic, fiscal and social benefits
19 driven by the industry will be fully realized.
20 3. The Legislature further finds and declares that the enactment
21 of this Act will achieve a bona fide public social and economic
22 purpose. The public investment made through the film infrastructure
23 transferable tax credits is intended to yield substantial benefits in
24 employment, workforce development and economic growth, and the
25 overall economic benefits expected to accrue from incremental
26 investment and the ongoing operations of the project will exceed
27 any adverse effect on public revenues from those tax incentives.
28 This Act, therefore, serves the public interest by fostering significant
29 new private investment, creating enduring jobs and educational
30 opportunities, and positioning Nevada as a leader in the content
31 creation industry while ensuring that the long-term gains to the
32 economy more than outweigh the State’s investment in the project.
33 Sec. 3. It is the intent of the Legislature, in enacting this Act,
34 to:
35 1. Promote the diversification of the economy of this State by
36 cultivating a thriving hub for content creation and production in
37 Nevada, which will establish Nevada as a nationally recognized
38 center for film, television and digital media production, thereby
39 broadening Nevada’s economic base beyond its traditional
40 industries and enhancing the State’s prominence in the creative
41 economy.
42 2. Provide an anchor for a new creative sector in Southern
43 Nevada through partnerships with global film and media companies
44 to develop and operate facilities for the production of film,
45 television and digital media productions and the involvement of
-
*AB5*
– 6 –
1 studio partners as anchor tenants to bring world-class expertise,
2 innovative technologies and global market access that will
3 accelerate the growth of a robust content creation industry in
4 Southern Nevada.
5 3. Support and promote workforce development in this State by
6 establishing and supporting education and vocational training
7 programs to prepare Nevada’s workforce for high-wage careers in
8 film, television and digital media production, equip Nevada’s
9 residents with in-demand skills and create pathways into the
10 industry, thereby generating thousands of new jobs for Nevadans
11 and building a skilled talent pool that sustains the State’s creative
12 sector for the long term.
13 Sec. 4. As used in sections 1 to 20, inclusive, of this act,
14 unless the context otherwise requires, the words and terms defined
15 in NRS 360.7582 and 360.7586, as amended by sections 24 and 25
16 of this act, have the meanings ascribed to them in those sections,
17 and the words and terms defined in sections 5 to 9, inclusive, of this
18 act have the meanings ascribed to them in those sections.
19 Sec. 5. “Capital investment” means all costs and expenses
20 incurred by the participants in the Project in connection with the
21 acquisition of the land for the Project and the acquisition,
22 construction, installation and equipping of the facilities, buildings,
23 structures and other infrastructure at the Project for the production
24 of qualified productions at the Project.
25 Sec. 6. “Lead participant” means the person designated by the
26 participants in the Project as the lead participant for the Project.
27 Sec. 7. “Nevada Partners Vocational Training Studio” means a
28 facility:
29 1. To be located by December 31, 2029, at a site owned by
30 Nevada Partners, Inc., or its successor organization, or if Nevada
31 Partners, Inc. ceases to exist and has no successor organization, to
32 be located by December 31, 2030, at a site approved by the
33 Southern Nevada Enterprise Community Board created by section 8
34 of the Southern Nevada Enterprise Community Infrastructure
35 Improvement Act; and
36 2. At which vocational training and education is to be provided
37 for the development of a trained workforce for the production in this
38 State of qualified productions that are film and television
39 productions.
40 Sec. 8. “Office” means the Office of Economic Development
41 within the Office of the Governor.
42 Sec. 9. “Summerlin Production Studios Project” or “Project”
43 means a project for the construction of a development consisting of
44 facilities, buildings, structures and other infrastructure for the
45 production of qualified productions at the site of real property
-

– 7 –
1 burdened by the following development agreements and owned by
2 the master developer under such development agreements or such

20 later than 2 years after the end of the period for which the

26 5. If the Office determines that the amount of direct production
27 expenditures is less than $150,000,000 in any fiscal year

35 fiscal year;
36 (b) Calculating a percentage by dividing the difference between
37 the $150,000,000 and the actual amount, as determined by the
38 Office, of direct production expenditures, by $150,000,000; and
39 (c) Multiplying the percentage calculated pursuant to paragraph
40 (b) by the amount calculated pursuant to paragraph (a).
41  Any penalty paid pursuant to this subsection must be applied to
42 reduce the amount of any penalty imposed pursuant to subsection 6.

34 more than 40 percent and not more than 50 percent less than the
35 applicable requirement for direct production expenditures included
36 in the development agreement pursuant to subparagraph (4) of
37 paragraph (a) of subsection 1, a penalty in the amount of
38 $40,000,000.
39 (g) If the actual amount of direct production expenditures is
40 more than 50 percent less than the applicable requirement for direct
41 production expenditures included in the development agreement
42 pursuant to subparagraph (4) of paragraph (a) of subsection 1, a
43 penalty in the amount of $50,000,000.
44 7. The Office may reduce, or waive, any penalty imposed
45 pursuant to subsections 3 to 6, inclusive, if, upon written request of
-
*AB5*
– 13 –
1 the lead participant, the Office determines that the failure to meet a
2 requirement for which a penalty may be imposed was caused by
3 extraordinary circumstances beyond the control of the Project and
4 reasonable, documented and good-faith efforts were made to satisfy
5 the requirement. For the purposes of this subsection, “extraordinary
6 circumstances”:
7 (a) Means natural disasters, labor strikes, significant disruptions
8 in material supply chains, substantial economic or geopolitical
9 shocks, government-mandated closures, delays in obtaining any
10 approval of a governmental entity needed for the Project that are not
11 caused by the Project or other events in the nature of force majeure
12 that materially impair the ability to carry out development and
13 construction activities.
14 (b) Does not include ordinary market fluctuations, internal
15 project scheduling decisions or changes in business strategy.

17 action authorized by subsection 7, the Executive Director of the
18 Office shall:
19 (a) Consider any documentation submitted by the production
20 company related to the action under consideration; and
21 (b) Make the following determinations in writing:
22 (1) That good cause exists to take such action; and
23 (2) That the action is reasonable based on the circumstances
24 of the underlying incident on which the reduction or withholding of
25 film infrastructure transferable tax credits authorized pursuant to

13 Sec. 12. 1. Except as otherwise provided in this subsection
14 and subsection 3, qualified direct production expenditures that may
15 serve as a basis for film infrastructure transferable tax credits issued
16 pursuant to section 11 of this act must:
17 (a) Be expenditures made during the period in which a qualified
18 production is produced;
19 (b) Be customary and reasonable;
20 (c) Relate to a category of qualified expenditures and costs listed
21 in subsection 2; and
22 (d) Be:
23 (1) Purchases, rentals or leases of tangible personal property
24 or services from a Nevada business.
25 (2) The payroll, including wages, salaries and fringe benefits,
26 for Nevada residents or other personnel for labor or services
27 provided in this State. The payroll, including wages, salaries and
28 fringe benefits, for Nevada residents or other personnel for labor or
29 services provided outside this State must not be a qualified direct
30 production expenditure.
31 (3) Compensation, including wages, salaries, fringe benefits
32 and other payments, paid to a bona fide third-party service provider,
33 or to another person receiving the compensation on behalf of the
34 bona fide third-party service provider, for labor or services provided
35 in Nevada. Compensation, including wages, salaries, fringe benefits
36 and other payments, paid to a bona fide third-party service provider,
37 or to another person receiving the compensation on behalf of the
38 bona fide third-party service provider, for labor or services provided
39 outside Nevada must not be a qualified direct production
40 expenditure.
41 2. Expenditures or costs that may serve as a basis for
42 calculating film infrastructure transferable tax credits must relate to:
43 (a) Set construction and operation;
44 (b) Wardrobe and makeup;
45 (c) Photography, sound and lighting;
-
*AB5*
– 20 –
1 (d) Filming, film processing and film editing;
2 (e) The rental or leasing of facilities, equipment and vehicles;
3 (f) Food and lodging;
4 (g) Editing, sound mixing, special effects, visual effects and
5 other postproduction services;
6 (h) Payment for goods or services provided by a Nevada
7 business;
8 (i) The design, construction, improvement or repair of property,
9 infrastructure, equipment or a production or postproduction facility;
10 (j) State and local government taxes to the extent not included as
11 part of another cost reported pursuant to this section; or
12 (k) Any other transaction, service or activity authorized in
13 regulations adopted by the Office pursuant to section 11 of this act.
14 3. Expenditures and costs:
15 (a) Related to:
16 (1) The acquisition, transfer or use of film infrastructure
17 transferable tax credits;
18 (2) Marketing and distribution;
19 (3) Financing, depreciation and amortization;
20 (4) The payment of any profits as a result of the qualified
21 production;
22 (5) The payment of the cost of the audit required by section
23 11 of this act; or
24 (6) The payment for any goods or services that are not
25 directly attributable to the qualified production;
26 (b) For which reimbursement is received, or for which
27 reimbursement is reasonably expected to be received;
28 (c) Which are paid to a joint venturer or a parent, subsidiary or
29 other affiliate of the production company, unless the amount paid
30 represents the fair market value, which may be represented by a rate
31 sheet, of the purchase, rental or lease of the property or services for
32 which payment is made;
33 (d) Which have been previously claimed as a basis for film
34 infrastructure transferable tax credits issued pursuant to section 11
35 of this act or noninfrastructure transferable tax credits issued
36 pursuant to NRS 360.759,
37  are not qualified direct production expenditures and are not
38 eligible to serve as a basis for film infrastructure transferable tax
39 credits issued pursuant to section 11 of this act.
40 4. If any tangible personal property is acquired by a Nevada
41 business from a vendor outside this State for immediate resale,

44 the purchase, rental or lease of the property are qualified direct
45 production expenditures only if:

1 (a) The Nevada business regularly deals in property of that kind;
2 (b) The expenditures are otherwise qualified direct production
3 expenditures under the provisions of this section; and
4 (c) Not more than 50 percent of the expenditures incurred by the
5 production company to purchase, rent or lease tangible personal
6 property for the qualified production are expenditures incurred for
7 the purchase, rental or lease of tangible personal property in the
8 manner described in this subsection. For the purposes of the
9 calculation required by this paragraph, the cost of any property that

19 6. As used in this section:
20 (a) “Bona fide third-party service provider” means a qualified
21 entity, a qualified individual or any other person determined by the
22 Office to be providing necessary and appropriate labor or services
23 directly related to the production.
24 (b) “Fringe benefits” means employee expenses paid by an
25 employer for the use of the employee’s services, including, without
26 limitation, payments made to a governmental entity, union dues,
27 health insurance premiums, payments to a pension plan and
28 payments for workers’ compensation insurance.
29 (c) “Qualified entity” means an entity that is:
30 (1) A personal service corporation, as defined in 26 U.S.C. §
31 269A(b)(1), a payroll services corporation or any entity receiving
32 payments for services performed in this State by a qualified
33 individual; and
34 (2) Registered to conduct business pursuant to the laws of
35 this State.
36 (d) “Qualified individual” means any natural person who
37 performs services during the production period in an activity related
38 to the production of a qualified production. The term does not
39 include:
40 (1) Any natural person related to the production company or
41 an employee as described in subparagraph (A), (B) or (C) of 26
42 U.S.C. § 51(i)(1).
43 (2) Any 5-percent owner, as defined in 26 U.S.C. §
44 416(i)(1)(B), of the production company.

1 Sec. 13. 1. Except as otherwise provided in subsections 3, 4

34 (7) Business affairs;
35 (8) Distribution; or
36 (9) Marketing and publicity.
37 3. The Executive Director of the Office shall waive a reduction
38 in the cumulative amount of film infrastructure transferable tax
39 credits required pursuant to subsection 2 upon written proof to the
40 Executive Director that the production company made a good faith
41 effort to meet the requirements of that paragraph and there is an
42 insufficient number of persons available and qualified to meet the
43 requirements.
44 4. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 5, the Executive
45 Director of the Office may:
-
*AB5*
– 26 –
1 (a) Reduce the cumulative amount of film infrastructure
2 transferable tax credits that are calculated pursuant to this section by
3 an amount equal to any damages incurred by the State or any
4 political subdivision of the State as a result of a qualified production
5 that is produced in this State; or
6 (b) Withhold film infrastructure transferable tax credits, in
7 whole or in part:
8 (1) Until any pending legal action in this State against a
9 production company or involving a qualified production is resolved.
10 (2) If a production company violates any state or local law.
11 (3) If a production company is found to have knowingly
12 submitted any false statement, representation or certification in any
13 document submitted for the purpose of obtaining film infrastructure
14 transferable tax credits.

16 Executive Director of the Office shall:
17 (a) Consider any documentation submitted by the production
18 company related to the action under consideration;
19 (b) Make the following determinations in writing:
20 (1) That good cause exists to take such action;
21 (2) That the action is reasonable based on the circumstances
22 of the underlying incident on which the reduction or withholding of
23 film infrastructure transferable tax credits authorized pursuant to
24 subsection 4 is based; and
25 (3) The amount of any reduction or withholding of film
26 infrastructure transferable tax credits authorized pursuant to
27 subsection 4 is commensurate with the severity of the underlying
28 incident on which the reduction or withholding is based; and
29 (c) Notify the production company, in writing, of the

32 (a) “Racial or ethnic minority” means persons who are:

37 (5) Middle Eastern or North African;
38 (6) Native Hawaiian;
39 (7) Pacific Islander; or

43 (1) Women;
44 (2) A racial or ethnic minority group;

1 (3) A group of persons who identify as LGBTQ, which

4 or expression;

6 NRS 426.068;
7 (5) Veterans;
8 (6) Persons who are currently serving on active duty in the

23 fiscal year beginning on or after July 1, 2029.

29 fiscal year may be carried forward and made available for approval
30 only during the next fiscal year, but the amount of film
31 infrastructure transferable tax credits carried forward and made
32 available for approval during the next fiscal year must not exceed
33 $47,500,000. For any fiscal year to which film infrastructure
34 transferable tax credits are carried forward from the immediately

35 Sec. 21. Chapter 353 of NRS is hereby amended by adding
36 thereto a new section to read as follows:
37 1. The Director of the Office of Finance in the Office of the
38 Governor shall submit a request to the State Board of Examiners
39 to suspend the authority of taxpayers to redeem film infrastructure
40 transferable tax credits issued pursuant to section 11 of this act or
41 noninfrastructure transferable tax credits issued pursuant to NRS
42 360.759, or both, if, at any time during a fiscal year, the Economic
43 Forum projects that the anticipated revenue of the State for that
44 fiscal year will fall short by 10 percent or more of the total
45 anticipated revenue for the fiscal year, as projected by the
-
*AB5*
– 36 –
1 Economic Forum for that fiscal year pursuant to paragraph (e) of
2 subsection 1 of NRS 353.228 and as adjusted by any legislation
3 enacted by the Legislature that affects state revenue for that fiscal
4 year.
5 2. The State Board of Examiners shall consider a request
6 made pursuant to subsection 1 and shall, if it finds that a
7 suspension is warranted based on the magnitude of the shortfall in
8 revenue, recommend to the Interim Finance Committee for its
9 independent evaluation and action that the suspension be imposed
10 for a period of time not to exceed 18 months after the date on
11 which the suspension is imposed. The Interim Finance Committee
12 is not bound to follow the recommendation of the State Board of
13 Examiners.
14 3. If the Interim Finance Committee finds that a suspension
15 recommended by the State Board of Examiners should and may
16 lawfully be made, the Committee shall by resolution direct the
17 Department of Taxation and the Nevada Gaming Control Board to
18 suspend the redemption of any film infrastructure transferable tax
19 credits issued pursuant to section 11 of this act or any
20 noninfrastructure transferable tax credits issued pursuant to NRS
21 360.759, or both, for a period of time not to exceed 18 months
22 after the date on which the suspension is imposed.
23 4. If a resolution is issued pursuant to subsection 3:
24 (a) The expiration date for film infrastructure transferable tax
25 credits set forth pursuant to section 15 of this act and
26 noninfrastructure transferable tax credits set forth pursuant to
27 NRS 360.7594, for which the suspension is imposed, must be
28 extended by the number of days that such transferable tax credits
29 may not be redeemed pursuant to the resolution.
30 (b) The total amount of film infrastructure transferable tax
31 credits set forth pursuant to section 15 of this act and
32 noninfrastructure transferable tax credits set forth pursuant to
33 NRS 360.7594 used by all taxpayers must not exceed 133 percent
34 of the total amount of film infrastructure transferable tax credits
35 pursuant to section 15 of this act and noninfrastructure
36 transferable tax credits pursuant to NRS 360.7594 authorized for
37 a fiscal year beginning on or after July 1, 2029, and before
38 June 30, 2044.
39 (c) For the purposes of paragraph (b), film infrastructure
40 transferable tax credits set forth pursuant to section 15 of this act
41 and noninfrastructure transferable tax credits set forth pursuant
42 to NRS 360.7594 must be accepted based on the date on which
43 they were issued, with the credits issued earliest in time accepted
44 until the limit set forth in paragraph (b) is met.

21 (d) Not less than 20 percent of the below-the-line personnel
22 employed on the qualified production, not including background
23 actors, are members of a traditionally underrepresented group.
24 (e) One or more entities affiliated with the production
25 company or distribution company has a program of substantive,
26 ongoing paid apprenticeships or internships that includes
27 members of traditionally underrepresented groups in not less than
28 three of the following departments:
29 (1) Production and development;
30 (2) Physical production;
31 (3) Postproduction;
32 (4) Music;
33 (5) Visual effects;
34 (6) Acquisitions;
35 (7) Business affairs;
36 (8) Distribution; or
37 (9) Marketing and publicity.
38 4. The Executive Director of the Office shall waive a
39 reduction in the cumulative amount of noninfrastructure
40 transferable tax credits required pursuant to subsection 3 upon
41 written proof to the Executive Director that the production
42 company made a good faith effort to meet the requirements of that
43 subsection and there is an insufficient number of persons
44 available and qualified to meet the requirements.
-
*AB5*
– 52 –
1 5. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 6, the
2 Executive Director of the Office may:
3 (a) Reduce the cumulative amount of noninfrastructure
4 transferable tax credits that are calculated pursuant to this section by
5 an amount equal to any damages incurred by the State or any
6 political subdivision of the State as a result of a qualified production
7 that is produced in this State; or
8 (b) Withhold the noninfrastructure transferable tax credits, in
9 whole or in part:
10 (1) Until any pending legal action in this State against a
11 production company or involving a qualified production is resolved.
12 (2) If a production company violates any state or local law.
13 (3) If a production company is found to have knowingly
14 submitted any false statement, representation or certification in any
15 document submitted for the purpose of obtaining noninfrastructure
16 transferable tax credits.
17 6. Before taking any action authorized by subsection 5, the
18 Executive Director of the Office shall:
19 (a) Consider any documentation submitted by the production
20 company related to the action under consideration; and
21 (b) Make the following determinations:
22 (1) That good cause exists to take such action;
23 (2) That the action is reasonable based on the
24 circumstances of the underlying incident on which the reduction
25 or withholding of noninfrastructure transferable tax credits
26 authorized pursuant to subsection 5 is based; and
27 (3) The amount of any reduction or withholding of
28 noninfrastructure transferable tax credits authorized pursuant to
29 subsection 5 is commensurate with severity of the underlying
30 incident on which the reduction or withholding is based.
31 7. As used in this section:
32 (a) “Racial or ethnic minority” means persons who are:
33 (1) Asian;
34 (2) Hispanic or Latino;
35 (3) Black or African American;
36 (4) Indigenous, Native American or Alaskan Native;
37 (5) Middle Eastern or North African;
38 (6) Native Hawaiian;
39 (7) Pacific Islander; or
40 (8) A member of any other underrepresented racial or
41 ethnic minority group.
42 (b) “Traditionally underrepresented group” means:
43 (1) Women;
44 (2) A racial or ethnic minority group;
-
*AB5*
– 53 –
1 (3) A group of persons who identify as LGBTQ, which
2 means lesbian, gay, bisexual, transgender, queer, intersex or any
3 other nonheterosexual or noncisgender orientation or gender
4 identity or expression;
5 (4) A group of persons with disabilities, as defined in
6 NRS 426.068;
7 (5) Veterans;
8 (6) Persons who are currently serving on active duty in the
9 Armed Forces of the United States; or
10 (7) Persons who were previously incarcerated in a jail or
11 prison.
12 (c) “Veteran” means a person who has served in the Armed
13 Forces of the United States, a reserve component thereof or the
14 National Guard and was separated from such service under
15 conditions other than dishonorable.

22 Sec. 33. Chapter 231 of NRS is hereby amended by adding
23 thereto the provisions set forth as sections 34 to 40, inclusive, of this
24 act.
25 Sec. 34. As used in sections 34 to 40, inclusive, of this act,
26 unless the context otherwise requires, the words and terms defined
27 in sections 35, 36 and 37 of this act have the meanings ascribed to
28 them in those sections.
29 Sec. 35. “Account” means the Account for Nevada Film,
30 Media and Related Technology Education and Vocational
31 Training created by section 38 of this act.
32 Sec. 36. “Board” means the Board for Nevada Film, Media
33 and Related Technology Education and Vocational Training
34 created by section 39 of this act.
35 Sec. 37. “Nevada Partners Vocational Training Studio” has
36 the meaning ascribed to it in section 7 of this act.
37 Sec. 38. 1. The Account for Nevada Film, Media and
38 Related Technology Education and Vocational Training is hereby
39 created in the State General Fund. The Executive Director of the
40 Office of Economic Development, at the direction of the Board,
41 shall administer the Account.
42 2. The Executive Director may apply for and accept gifts,
43 grants, bequests and donations from any source for deposit in the
44 Account.
45 3. The Account consists of:
-
*AB5*
– 59 –
1 (a) Money transferred to the Account pursuant to NRS
2 360.759 and section 11 of this act.
3 (b) Any direct legislative appropriations to the Account.
4 (c) Any gifts, grants, bequests and donations made to the
5 Account.
6 (d) Interest and income earned on money in the Account.
7 4. The interest and income earned on the money in the
8 Account, after deducting any applicable charges, must be credited
9 to the Account.
10 5. Any money remaining in the Account at the end of the
11 fiscal year does not revert to the State General Fund, and the
12 balance in the Account must be carried forward to the next fiscal
13 year.
14 6. Money in the Account must be used by the Office to make
15 grants to any institution within the Nevada System of Higher
16 Education, a state or local agency, a school district, a charter
17 school, a vocational trade school, a nonprofit organization, a labor
18 organization or a private postsecondary educational institution
19 that provides a program of workforce development for the
20 production of qualified productions in this State. Thirty percent of
21 the money which is distributed from the Account in the form of
22 grants must be allocated to the Nevada Partners Vocational
23 Training Studio for the operation and overhead costs of the
24 Nevada Partners Vocational Training Studio. Seventy percent of
25 the money which is distributed from the Account in the form of
26 grants must be allocated to educational and vocational training
27 organizations pursuant to section 40 of this act for the purpose of
28 providing programs of workforce development for the production
29 of qualified productions in this State.
30 7. As used in this section, “qualified production” has the
31 meaning ascribed to it in NRS 360.7586.
32 Sec. 39. 1. There is hereby created the Board for Nevada
33 Film, Media and Related Technology Education and Vocational
34 Training within the Office of Economic Development in the Office
35 of the Governor, consisting of the following voting members:
36 (a) One member appointed by the Governor;
37 (b) One member, who must not be a Legislator, appointed by
38 the Majority Leader of the Senate;
39 (c) One member, who must not be a Legislator, appointed by
40 the Speaker of the Assembly;
41 (d) One member, who must not be a Legislator, appointed by
42 the Minority Leader of the Senate;
43 (e) One member, who must not be a Legislator, appointed by
44 the Minority Leader of the Assembly;
-
*AB5*
– 60 –
1 (f) Two members appointed by the Governor from nominees
2 selected by the lead participant in the Summerlin Production
3 Studios Project;
4 (g) One member appointed by the Governor from a nominee
5 selected by the Southern Nevada Enterprise Community Board to
6 represent the interests of the Nevada Partners Vocational Training
7 Studio;
8 (h) One member appointed by the Board of Regents of the
9 University of Nevada;
10 (i) The President of the University of Nevada, Las Vegas, or
11 his or her designee; and
12 (j) The President of the University of Nevada, Reno, or his or
13 her designee.
14 2. In appointing members to the Board pursuant to
15 subsection 1, the appointing authorities set forth in that subsection
16 shall coordinate to ensure that both the public and private sectors
17 are represented on the Board.
18 3. The members appointed pursuant to paragraphs (a), (c),
19 (e) and (g) of subsection 1, and one member appointed pursuant to
20 paragraph (f) of subsection 1, must be appointed to an initial term
21 of 2 years commencing on January 1, 2028, and the members
22 appointed pursuant to paragraphs (b), (d) and (h) of subsection 1,
23 and one member appointed pursuant to paragraph (f) of
24 subsection 1, must be appointed to an initial term of 4 years
25 commencing on January 1, 2028. After the initial terms, each
26 appointed member shall serve a term of 4 years. Each appointed
27 member serves at the pleasure of the person appointing that
28 member pursuant to subsection 1. If, for any reason, a vacancy
29 occurs during the term of an appointed member, the person who is
30 responsible for making the appointment pursuant to subsection 1
31 shall appoint a replacement qualified pursuant to that subsection
32 to serve for the remainder of the unexpired term. Each appointed
33 member may serve not more than three consecutive full terms.
34 4. At the first meeting of each fiscal year, the Board shall
35 elect from among its members a Chair and a Vice Chair. The
36 Executive Director of the Office of Economic Development shall
37 serve as the nonvoting Secretary of the Board.
38 5. A majority of the voting members of the Board constitutes
39 a quorum, and the affirmative vote of a majority of the voting
40 members of the Board is required to exercise any power conferred
41 on the Board.
42 6. The Board shall meet at least twice each calendar year but
43 may meet more often at the call of the Chair or a majority of the
44 voting members of the Board.

1 7. The members of the Board serve without compensation but

Raw Text:
A.B. 5
ASSEMBLY BILL NO. 5–SELECT COMMITTEE
ON JOBS AND ECONOMY
PREFILED NOVEMBER 12, 2025
____________
Referred to Select Committee on Jobs and Economy
SUMMARY—Enacts the Nevada Studio Infrastructure Jobs and
Workforce Training Act. (BDR S-13)
FISCAL NOTE: Effect on Local Government: May have Fiscal Impact.
Effect on the State: Yes.
~
EXPLANATION – Matter in bolded italics is new; matter between brackets [omitted material] is material to be omitted.
AN ACT relating to economic development; enacting the Nevada
Studio Infrastructure Jobs and Workforce Training Act;
requiring the Office of Economic Development to enter
into a development agreement to establish certain criteria
for the development of infrastructure for the production of
motion pictures and other qualified productions and other
new capital investment in this State; establishing certain
penalties if the development does not meet certain
requirements for new capital investment and expenditures
for the production of motion pictures and other qualified
productions; establishing requirements for a production
company located at such a development to be eligible for
film infrastructure transferable tax credits for qualified
productions produced at the development; providing for
the calculation of the amount of film infrastructure
transferable tax credits; requiring the creation of a
production studio entertainment district; revising
provisions governing noninfrastructure transferable tax
credits for motion pictures and other qualified productions
produced in this State; authorizing an additional amount
of noninfrastructure transferable tax credits; establishing
the Account for Nevada Film, Media and Related
Technology Education and Vocational Training and a
board to approve distributions from the Account;
providing for the distribution of money from the Account
-
*AB5*

– 2 –
to certain entities and organizations that provide
education and vocational training to develop a workforce
for the production of qualified productions in this State;
and providing other matters properly relating thereto.
Legislative Counsel’s Digest:
1 Existing law establishes a program for the issuance of transferable tax credits
2 by the Office of Economic Development to the production company of a motion
3 picture or other qualified production, based upon qualified direct production
4 expenditures made for the purchase of personal property or services from a Nevada
5 business. (NRS 360.758-360.7598) This bill revises provisions governing these
6 transferable tax credits and enacts the Nevada Studio Infrastructure Jobs and
7 Workforce Training Act to authorize film infrastructure transferable tax credits for
8 qualified productions produced at the site of the Summerlin Production Studios
9 Project.
10 Sections 1-20 of this bill enact the Nevada Studio Infrastructure Jobs and
11 Workforce Training Act, which provides film infrastructure transferable tax credits
12 for production companies located within the Summerlin Production Studios Project,
13 as defined in section 9. Section 10 requires the Office of Economic Development
14 to enter into a development agreement with the lead participant of the Project to
15 establish: (1) certain criteria that the Project is required to satisfy for film
16 infrastructure transferable tax credits to be authorized for qualified productions at
17 the Project; and (2) certain requirements for new capital investment in this State
18 and the generation of direct production expenditures in this State, which the Project
19 must meet, with certain exceptions, to avoid penalties specified in section 10.
20 Section 11: (1) authorizes production companies located at the Project to apply, on
21 or after December 1, 2026, to the Office for film infrastructure transferable tax
22 credits for qualified productions produced, in whole or in part, at the Project; and
23 (2) authorizes such credits to be used against the modified business tax, insurance
24 premium tax or gaming license fee, or any combination of these taxes and fees.
25 Section 12 establishes the qualified direct production expenditures which are the
26 basis for calculating the amount of film infrastructure transferable tax credits,
27 including, without limitation: (1) purchases, rentals or leases of property or services
28 from a Nevada business; (2) wages and fringe benefits paid to employees who are
29 Nevada residents or other personnel for labor or services provided in this State on
30 the qualified production; and (3) amounts paid to service providers for the services
31 of certain persons on the qualified production. Section 13 establishes requirements
32 for the employment of Nevada residents as below-the-line employees of qualified
33 productions. Section 14 provides that the base amount of film infrastructure
34 transferable tax credits is 30 percent of the amount of qualified direct production
35 expenditures calculated under section 12, with certain reductions if the production
36 company does not satisfy certain criteria for work opportunities to members of
37 traditionally underrepresented groups. Section 15: (1) limits the total amount of
38 film infrastructure transferable tax credits issued pursuant to sections 1-20 to
39 $95,000,000 for each fiscal year beginning on or after July 1, 2029; and (2)
40 prohibits the approval of an application for film infrastructure transferable tax
41 credits if the application is submitted in a fiscal year that begins on or after July 1,
42 2044. Section 16 requires a production company to: (1) commence principal
43 photography within a certain period of time after the Office approves an application
44 for a certificate of eligibility for film infrastructure transferable tax credits; (2)
45 complete the qualified production within 18 months after the date of
46 commencement of principal photography, except that the Office may extend this
47 period for not more than 6 months; and (3) submit certain required information
48 within the required period. Section 17 requires a production company to repay film
-
*AB5*

– 3 –
49 infrastructure transferable tax credits under certain circumstances. Section 19
50 requires the lead participant in the Project to submit certain reports to the Governor,
51 the Legislature and the Office. Section 20 requires certain reports to be made to the
52 Legislature concerning film infrastructure transferable tax credits.
53 Sections 23-32 of this bill make various changes to the existing law governing
54 the noninfrastructure transferable tax credits for motion picture and other qualified
55 productions. (NRS 360.758-360.7598) Section 24 changes references to “extras” in
56 a qualification production to “background actors.” Section 25: (1) provides that
57 digital media productions are qualified productions for the purposes of eligibility
58 for film infrastructure transferable tax credits and noninfrastructure transferable tax
59 credits; and (2) clarifies that media productions solely produced for social media
60 are not eligible for such transferable tax credits. Section 26 revises the criteria to be
61 eligible for noninfrastructure transferable tax credits to be the same as the criteria
62 for film infrastructure transferable tax credits by: (1) removing the requirement that
63 a certain percentage of direct production expenditures be incurred in this State and,
64 instead, requiring that at least 50 percent of the total principal photography days of
65 the qualified production take place in this State or a certain amount of qualified
66 direct production expenditures be incurred in this State; and (2) requiring a
67 production company to have a workforce plan that establishes certain goals and
68 provide to the Office a final assessment of whether the production company met or
69 made a good faith effort to meet those goals. Section 22 of this bill applies to
70 applicants for noninfrastructure transferable tax credits the same requirements for
71 the employment of Nevada residents as below-the-line personnel that apply to
72 applicants for film infrastructure transferable tax credits. Section 27 revises the
73 expenditures and costs that may serve as a basis for noninfrastructure transferable
74 tax credits. Section 28: (1) increases the base amount of transferable tax credits
75 from 15 percent of the qualified direct production expenditures to 30 percent of the
76 qualified direct production expenditures, for an application submitted in each fiscal
77 year beginning on or after July 1, 2029, and ending before July 1, 2044; and (2)
78 provides for certain reductions to that base amount during that period. Section 29
79 makes certain provisions of existing law relating to the calculation of
80 noninfrastructure transferable tax credits inapplicable for the period beginning on
81 July 1, 2029, and ending on June 30, 2044. Section 30 temporarily increases from
82 $10,000,000 to $25,000,000 the total amount of noninfrastructure transferable tax
83 credits for motion picture and other qualified productions that may be issued under
84 the existing program for each fiscal year beginning on or after July 1, 2029, until
85 June 30, 2044. Sections 31 and 32 make conforming changes so that
86 noninfrastructure transferable tax credits are administered and reported in the same
87 manner as film infrastructure transferable tax credits.
88 Section 18 requires the Clark County Board of County Commissioners to
89 create a production studio entertainment district for the purpose of enhancing early
90 childhood education opportunities, including prekindergarten, for children in Clark
91 County. Under section 18, the boundaries of the district are required to be entirely
92 within the unincorporated areas of Clark County and include only parcels of land
93 that are located within the boundaries of the Summerlin Production Studios Project.
94 Section 18 requires certain taxes on transient lodging, certain property taxes and
95 certain sales and use taxes imposed in the district to be pledged and distributed to
96 the Clark County School District and used by the Clark County School District
97 solely for the purposes of prekindergarten programs in the Clark County School
98 District. Finally, section 18 requires the Clark County School District to submit
99 annual reports to the Office concerning the use of money distributed to Clark
100 County School District under section 18.
101 Sections 33-40 of this bill establish a program to provide grants to certain
102 organizations that provide education and vocational training for workforce
103 development for the production of motion pictures and other qualified productions.
-
*AB5*

– 4 –
104 Section 38 establishes the Account for Nevada Film, Media and Related
105 Technology Education and Vocational Training for the purpose of allocating
106 money to certain entities and organizations that provide education and vocational
107 training for such workforce development. Sections 11 and 26 require a production
108 company that is issued transferable tax credits for a qualified production to pay to
109 the Office an amount of money equal to 1 percentage point of the percent of
110 qualified direct production expenditures used to calculate the amount of
111 transferable tax credits issued to the qualified production, and requires the Office to
112 deposit that money with the State Treasurer for credit to the Account. Section 39
113 creates and provides for the composition of the Board for Nevada Film, Media and
114 Related Technology Education and Vocational Training within the Office of
115 Economic Development. Section 40: (1) requires the Board to establish the
116 procedure for a person or entity to apply for a grant of money from the Account, the
117 criteria to be used to determine whether to approve an application for a grant from
118 the Account to an applicant and the requirements for reports by recipients of such
119 grants concerning the use of the grants; and (2) prohibits the making of a grant from
120 the Account unless the Board approves the application for the grant.
THE PEOPLE OF THE STATE OF NEVADA, REPRESENTED IN
SENATE AND ASSEMBLY, DO ENACT AS FOLLOWS:
1 Section 1. Sections 1 to 20, inclusive, of this act may be cited
2 as the Nevada Studio Infrastructure Jobs and Workforce Training
3 Act.
4 Sec. 2. 1. The Legislature hereby finds and declares that:
5 (a) The Las Vegas Metropolitan Area is the largest metropolitan
6 area in this State and has a site available to be developed to create
7 large-scale facilities for the location of companies that produce
8 motion pictures, television programs and other qualified productions
9 in this State. The establishment of such a studio campus will create
10 jobs in Nevada’s creative industries and diversify the economy of
11 this State.
12 (b) The Las Vegas Metropolitan Area possesses unique
13 geographic, economic and resource advantages that make it
14 especially suitable for a project of this magnitude. Because of these
15 unique local conditions, it is necessary to enact a law of local and
16 special application to promote and secure the benefits of a large-
17 scale film and media production development in Southern Nevada
18 for the benefit of the entire State.
19 (c) Because of these special characteristics and circumstances in
20 Southern Nevada, a general law cannot be made applicable to
21 achieve the purposes of this Act and a law of local and special
22 application is necessary to promote and secure the advantages of the
23 local and special characteristics and circumstances within the Las
24 Vegas Metropolitan Area.
25 2. The Legislature further finds and declares that the content
26 production industry has presented an ambitious and visionary plan
-
*AB5*

– 5 –
1 for all of Southern Nevada, which leverages the region’s unique
2 geographic assets, economic capabilities and infrastructural
3 advantages. The industry’s vision will promote the generation of
4 thousands of high-quality, high-paying jobs, billions of dollars in
5 incremental capital investments and billions more in new economic
6 output and ongoing spending. This plan transcends the development
7 of a mere studio complex, proposing instead a dynamic production
8 campus that is intended to serve as the nucleus for a robust,
9 sustainable industrial cluster. The Legislature recognizes that
10 realizing this vision depends fundamentally upon a collaborative
11 public-private partnership, wherein the State’s commitment,
12 provided through transferable tax credits, creates leverage that
13 significantly multiplies the benefits accruing to this State. In
14 entering this partnership, the Legislature affirms its clear and
15 unwavering expectation that if the industry benefits from the State’s
16 contribution of transferable tax credits, the industry’s promises will
17 be fulfilled, the outcomes articulated by the industry will be met or
18 exceeded, and the anticipated economic, fiscal and social benefits
19 driven by the industry will be fully realized.
20 3. The Legislature further finds and declares that the enactment
21 of this Act will achieve a bona fide public social and economic
22 purpose. The public investment made through the film infrastructure
23 transferable tax credits is intended to yield substantial benefits in
24 employment, workforce development and economic growth, and the
25 overall economic benefits expected to accrue from incremental
26 investment and the ongoing operations of the project will exceed
27 any adverse effect on public revenues from those tax incentives.
28 This Act, therefore, serves the public interest by fostering significant
29 new private investment, creating enduring jobs and educational
30 opportunities, and positioning Nevada as a leader in the content
31 creation industry while ensuring that the long-term gains to the
32 economy more than outweigh the State’s investment in the project.
33 Sec. 3. It is the intent of the Legislature, in enacting this Act,
34 to:
35 1. Promote the diversification of the economy of this State by
36 cultivating a thriving hub for content creation and production in
37 Nevada, which will establish Nevada as a nationally recognized
38 center for film, television and digital media production, thereby
39 broadening Nevada’s economic base beyond its traditional
40 industries and enhancing the State’s prominence in the creative
41 economy.
42 2. Provide an anchor for a new creative sector in Southern
43 Nevada through partnerships with global film and media companies
44 to develop and operate facilities for the production of film,
45 television and digital media productions and the involvement of
-
*AB5*

– 6 –
1 studio partners as anchor tenants to bring world-class expertise,
2 innovative technologies and global market access that will
3 accelerate the growth of a robust content creation industry in
4 Southern Nevada.
5 3. Support and promote workforce development in this State by
6 establishing and supporting education and vocational training
7 programs to prepare Nevada’s workforce for high-wage careers in
8 film, television and digital media production, equip Nevada’s
9 residents with in-demand skills and create pathways into the
10 industry, thereby generating thousands of new jobs for Nevadans
11 and building a skilled talent pool that sustains the State’s creative
12 sector for the long term.
13 Sec. 4. As used in sections 1 to 20, inclusive, of this act,
14 unless the context otherwise requires, the words and terms defined
15 in NRS 360.7582 and 360.7586, as amended by sections 24 and 25
16 of this act, have the meanings ascribed to them in those sections,
17 and the words and terms defined in sections 5 to 9, inclusive, of this
18 act have the meanings ascribed to them in those sections.
19 Sec. 5. “Capital investment” means all costs and expenses
20 incurred by the participants in the Project in connection with the
21 acquisition of the land for the Project and the acquisition,
22 construction, installation and equipping of the facilities, buildings,
23 structures and other infrastructure at the Project for the production
24 of qualified productions at the Project.
25 Sec. 6. “Lead participant” means the person designated by the
26 participants in the Project as the lead participant for the Project.
27 Sec. 7. “Nevada Partners Vocational Training Studio” means a
28 facility:
29 1. To be located by December 31, 2029, at a site owned by
30 Nevada Partners, Inc., or its successor organization, or if Nevada
31 Partners, Inc. ceases to exist and has no successor organization, to
32 be located by December 31, 2030, at a site approved by the
33 Southern Nevada Enterprise Community Board created by section 8
34 of the Southern Nevada Enterprise Community Infrastructure
35 Improvement Act; and
36 2. At which vocational training and education is to be provided
37 for the development of a trained workforce for the production in this
38 State of qualified productions that are film and television
39 productions.
40 Sec. 8. “Office” means the Office of Economic Development
41 within the Office of the Governor.
42 Sec. 9. “Summerlin Production Studios Project” or “Project”
43 means a project for the construction of a development consisting of
44 facilities, buildings, structures and other infrastructure for the
45 production of qualified productions at the site of real property
-
*AB5*

– 7 –
1 burdened by the following development agreements and owned by
2 the master developer under such development agreements or such
3 master developer’s affiliated entities:
4 1. Development agreement between Clark County and Howard
5 Hughes Properties, Limited Partnership dated February 7, 1996, as
6 amended, and recorded on September 4, 1996, in Book 960904 as
7 Instrument No. 01725 and re-recorded on September 10, 1996, in
8 Book 960910 as Instrument No. 01379 in the official records of the
9 Clark County, Nevada Recorder’s Office.
10 2. Development agreement between the City of Las Vegas and
11 Howard Hughes Properties, Limited Partnership, recorded on
12 November 21, 1997, in Book 971121 as Instrument No. 00839, as
13 amended, in the official records of the Clark County, Nevada
14 Recorder’s Office.
15 Sec. 10. 1. Not later than 120 days after the effective date of
16 this act, the Office shall enter into a development agreement with
17 the lead participant of the Summerlin Production Studios Project,
18 unless the Office agrees to extend this period by not more than 60
19 days. The development agreement entered into pursuant to this
20 section:
21 (a) Must require the Project to:
22 (1) Except as otherwise provided in subsections 2 and 3, not
23 later than:
24 (I) December 31, 2028, make a new capital investment in
25 this State, excluding any hotel and any business required to hold a
26 license issued pursuant to chapter 463 of NRS, of at least
27 $400,000,000.
28 (II) June 30, 2030, make an aggregate new capital
29 investment in this State, of at least $900,000,000. For the purposes
30 of determining the amount of new capital investment pursuant to
31 this sub-subparagraph, any new capital investment by a third party
32 who purchases property or enters into a ground lease for property
33 within the site of the Project must be credited toward meeting the
34 requirement of this sub-subparagraph. The Office shall credit toward
35 meeting the requirement of this sub-subparagraph 50 percent of the
36 new capital investment made at the Downtown Summerlin site
37 during the period beginning on the date of the execution of the
38 development agreement and ending on June 30, 2030, if the Board
39 of Economic Development determines that the new capital
40 investment is consistent with the State Plan for Economic
41 Development developed by the Executive Director of the Office of
42 Economic Development pursuant to subsection 2 of NRS 231.053
43 and the intent of the Legislature as expressed in sections 2 and 3 of
44 this act.

11 3. If the Office determines that the Project has not met a
12 requirement for capital investment included in the development
13 agreement pursuant to subparagraph (1) of paragraph (a) of
14 subsection 1, the Office must document its determination in writing,
15 notify the lead participant, in writing, of its determination and
16 impose a penalty on the Project in an amount not to exceed the
17 amount of the deficiency. The Project may cure the deficiency by
18 making the required capital investment in the element of the Project
19 for which the requirement for capital investment was not met not
20 later than 2 years after the end of the period for which the
21 requirement for capital investment was not met, in an amount
22 necessary to satisfy the requirement for capital investment in an
23 element of the Project that was not met. If the deficiency is:
24 (a) Cured within the cure period, 100 percent of the amount of
25 the penalty must be discharged.
26 (b) Not cured within that cure period, the Office must record a
27 lien on any land within the Project that is undeveloped or has not
28 been developed in accordance with the findings and intent of the
29 Legislature as expressed in sections 2 and 3 of this act, to secure
30 payment of such penalty, subject to the limitations set forth in
31 subsection 4. Any penalty, and the lien securing the payment of such
32 penalty, must be discharged as follows:
33 (1) If the requirement for capital investment which was not
34 met is satisfied not later than 1 year after the expiration of the cure
35 period, 90 percent of the amount of the penalty, and the lien
36 securing the payment of the penalty, must be discharged.
37 (2) If the requirement for capital investment which was not
38 met is satisfied more than 1 year, but not later than 2 years, after the
39 expiration of the cure period, 70 percent of the amount of the
40 penalty, and the lien securing the payment of the penalty, must be
41 discharged.
42 (3) If the requirement for capital investment which was not
43 met is satisfied more than 2 years, but not later than 3 years, after
44 the expiration of the cure period, 50 percent of the amount of the
-
*AB5*

– 11 –
1 penalty, and the lien securing the payment of the penalty, must be
2 discharged.
3 (4) If the requirement for capital investment which was not
4 met is satisfied more than 3 years, but not later than 4 years, after
5 the expiration of the cure period, 30 percent of the amount of the
6 penalty, and the lien securing the payment of the penalty, must be
7 discharged.
8 (5) If the requirement for capital investment which was not
9 met is satisfied more than 4 years, but not later than 5 years, after
10 the expiration of the cure period, 10 percent of the amount of the
11 penalty, and the lien securing the payment of the penalty, must be
12 discharged.
13 4. Only one lien may by recorded pursuant to subsection 3 and
14 such a lien:
15 (a) Must not, at any time, exceed the lesser of the amount of the
16 deficiency or 100 percent of the appraised value of the remaining
17 land within the Project that is undeveloped or has not been
18 developed in accordance with the findings and intent of the
19 Legislature as expressed in sections 2 and 3 of this act.
20 (b) May not be recorded on any completed portion of the
21 Project.
22 (c) May be modified, replaced or reissued to secure payment of
23 the most current amount of any penalty imposed pursuant to
24 subsection 3 but any such lien is subject to the limitations of this
25 subsection.
26 5. If the Office determines that the amount of direct production
27 expenditures is less than $150,000,000 in any fiscal year
28 commencing on or after July 1, 2029, and before July 1, 2044, the
29 Office must notify the Project, in writing, of its determination and
30 impose a penalty on the Project in an amount equal to the lesser of
31 $10,000,000 or the amount determined by:
32 (a) Calculating 50 percent of the sum of the film infrastructure
33 transferable tax credits authorized for approval pursuant to section
34 15 of this act for that fiscal year and the immediately preceding
35 fiscal year;
36 (b) Calculating a percentage by dividing the difference between
37 the $150,000,000 and the actual amount, as determined by the
38 Office, of direct production expenditures, by $150,000,000; and
39 (c) Multiplying the percentage calculated pursuant to paragraph
40 (b) by the amount calculated pursuant to paragraph (a).
41  Any penalty paid pursuant to this subsection must be applied to
42 reduce the amount of any penalty imposed pursuant to subsection 6.

13 Sec. 12. 1. Except as otherwise provided in this subsection
14 and subsection 3, qualified direct production expenditures that may
15 serve as a basis for film infrastructure transferable tax credits issued
16 pursuant to section 11 of this act must:
17 (a) Be expenditures made during the period in which a qualified
18 production is produced;
19 (b) Be customary and reasonable;
20 (c) Relate to a category of qualified expenditures and costs listed
21 in subsection 2; and
22 (d) Be:
23 (1) Purchases, rentals or leases of tangible personal property
24 or services from a Nevada business.
25 (2) The payroll, including wages, salaries and fringe benefits,
26 for Nevada residents or other personnel for labor or services
27 provided in this State. The payroll, including wages, salaries and
28 fringe benefits, for Nevada residents or other personnel for labor or
29 services provided outside this State must not be a qualified direct
30 production expenditure.
31 (3) Compensation, including wages, salaries, fringe benefits
32 and other payments, paid to a bona fide third-party service provider,
33 or to another person receiving the compensation on behalf of the
34 bona fide third-party service provider, for labor or services provided
35 in Nevada. Compensation, including wages, salaries, fringe benefits
36 and other payments, paid to a bona fide third-party service provider,
37 or to another person receiving the compensation on behalf of the
38 bona fide third-party service provider, for labor or services provided
39 outside Nevada must not be a qualified direct production
40 expenditure.
41 2. Expenditures or costs that may serve as a basis for
42 calculating film infrastructure transferable tax credits must relate to:
43 (a) Set construction and operation;
44 (b) Wardrobe and makeup;
45 (c) Photography, sound and lighting;
-
*AB5*

– 20 –
1 (d) Filming, film processing and film editing;
2 (e) The rental or leasing of facilities, equipment and vehicles;
3 (f) Food and lodging;
4 (g) Editing, sound mixing, special effects, visual effects and
5 other postproduction services;
6 (h) Payment for goods or services provided by a Nevada
7 business;
8 (i) The design, construction, improvement or repair of property,
9 infrastructure, equipment or a production or postproduction facility;
10 (j) State and local government taxes to the extent not included as
11 part of another cost reported pursuant to this section; or
12 (k) Any other transaction, service or activity authorized in
13 regulations adopted by the Office pursuant to section 11 of this act.
14 3. Expenditures and costs:
15 (a) Related to:
16 (1) The acquisition, transfer or use of film infrastructure
17 transferable tax credits;
18 (2) Marketing and distribution;
19 (3) Financing, depreciation and amortization;
20 (4) The payment of any profits as a result of the qualified
21 production;
22 (5) The payment of the cost of the audit required by section
23 11 of this act; or
24 (6) The payment for any goods or services that are not
25 directly attributable to the qualified production;
26 (b) For which reimbursement is received, or for which
27 reimbursement is reasonably expected to be received;
28 (c) Which are paid to a joint venturer or a parent, subsidiary or
29 other affiliate of the production company, unless the amount paid
30 represents the fair market value, which may be represented by a rate
31 sheet, of the purchase, rental or lease of the property or services for
32 which payment is made;
33 (d) Which have been previously claimed as a basis for film
34 infrastructure transferable tax credits issued pursuant to section 11
35 of this act or noninfrastructure transferable tax credits issued
36 pursuant to NRS 360.759,
37  are not qualified direct production expenditures and are not
38 eligible to serve as a basis for film infrastructure transferable tax
39 credits issued pursuant to section 11 of this act.
40 4. If any tangible personal property is acquired by a Nevada
41 business from a vendor outside this State for immediate resale,
42 rental or lease to a production company that produces a qualified

44 the purchase, rental or lease of the property are qualified direct
45 production expenditures only if:

– 21 –
1 (a) The Nevada business regularly deals in property of that kind;
2 (b) The expenditures are otherwise qualified direct production
3 expenditures under the provisions of this section; and
4 (c) Not more than 50 percent of the expenditures incurred by the
5 production company to purchase, rent or lease tangible personal
6 property for the qualified production are expenditures incurred for
7 the purchase, rental or lease of tangible personal property in the
8 manner described in this subsection. For the purposes of the
9 calculation required by this paragraph, the cost of any property that

13 described in this subsection.

19 6. As used in this section:
20 (a) “Bona fide third-party service provider” means a qualified
21 entity, a qualified individual or any other person determined by the
22 Office to be providing necessary and appropriate labor or services
23 directly related to the production.
24 (b) “Fringe benefits” means employee expenses paid by an
25 employer for the use of the employee’s services, including, without
26 limitation, payments made to a governmental entity, union dues,
27 health insurance premiums, payments to a pension plan and
28 payments for workers’ compensation insurance.
29 (c) “Qualified entity” means an entity that is:
30 (1) A personal service corporation, as defined in 26 U.S.C. §
31 269A(b)(1), a payroll services corporation or any entity receiving
32 payments for services performed in this State by a qualified
33 individual; and
34 (2) Registered to conduct business pursuant to the laws of
35 this State.
36 (d) “Qualified individual” means any natural person who
37 performs services during the production period in an activity related
38 to the production of a qualified production. The term does not
39 include:
40 (1) Any natural person related to the production company or
41 an employee as described in subparagraph (A), (B) or (C) of 26
42 U.S.C. § 51(i)(1).
43 (2) Any 5-percent owner, as defined in 26 U.S.C. §
44 416(i)(1)(B), of the production company.
