1 Sec. 13. 1. Except as otherwise provided in subsections 3, 4
2 and 5, the Office shall not issue film infrastructure transferable tax
3 credits to a production company pursuant to section 11 of this
4 act unless, in addition to meeting any other requirements for
5 the issuance of film infrastructure transferable tax credits, the
6 production company satisfies the applicable requirement for the
7 employment of Nevada residents as below-the-line personnel of
8 the qualified production as follows:
9 (a) For a qualified production that submits an application for a
10 certificate of eligibility for film infrastructure transferable tax
11 credits pursuant to section 11 of this act on or after July 1, 2026, and
12 before July 1, 2027, at least 10 percent of the below-the-line
13 personnel of the qualified production are Nevada residents.
14 (b) For a qualified production that submits an application for a
15 certificate of eligibility for film infrastructure transferable tax
16 credits pursuant to section 11 of this act on or after July 1, 2027, and
17 before July 1, 2028, at least 15 percent of the below-the-line
18 personnel of the qualified production are Nevada residents.
19 (c) For a qualified production that submits an application for a
20 certificate of eligibility for film infrastructure transferable tax
21 credits pursuant to section 11 of this act on or after July 1, 2028, and
22 before July 1, 2029, at least 20 percent of the below-the-line
23 personnel of the qualified production are Nevada residents.
24 (d) For a qualified production that submits an application for a
25 certificate of eligibility for film infrastructure transferable tax
26 credits pursuant to section 11 of this act on or after July 1, 2029, and
27 before July 1, 2030, at least 25 percent of the below-the-line
28 personnel of the qualified production are Nevada residents.
29 (e) For a qualified production that submits an application for a
30 certificate of eligibility for film infrastructure transferable tax
31 credits pursuant to section 11 of this act on or after July 1, 2030, and
32 before July 1, 2031, at least 30 percent of the below-the-line
33 personnel of the qualified production are Nevada residents.
34 (f) For a qualified production that submits an application for a
35 certificate of eligibility for film infrastructure transferable tax
36 credits pursuant to section 11 of this act on or after July 1, 2031, and
37 before July 1, 2032, at least 40 percent of the below-the-line
38 personnel of the qualified production are Nevada residents.
39 (g) For a qualified production that submits an application for a
40 certificate of eligibility for film infrastructure transferable tax
41 credits pursuant to section 11 of this act on or after July 1, 2032, and
42 before July 1, 2038, at least 50 percent of the below-the-line
43 personnel of the qualified production are Nevada residents.

21 provided in this State by a denominator consisting of the total wages
22 and salaries paid to all below-the-line personnel, excluding

43 (1) Women;

7 (5) Veterans;
8 (6) Persons who are currently serving on active duty in the

35 Sec. 21. Chapter 353 of NRS is hereby amended by adding
36 thereto a new section to read as follows:
37 1. The Director of the Office of Finance in the Office of the
38 Governor shall submit a request to the State Board of Examiners
39 to suspend the authority of taxpayers to redeem film infrastructure
40 transferable tax credits issued pursuant to section 11 of this act or
41 noninfrastructure transferable tax credits issued pursuant to NRS
42 360.759, or both, if, at any time during a fiscal year, the Economic
43 Forum projects that the anticipated revenue of the State for that
44 fiscal year will fall short by 10 percent or more of the total
45 anticipated revenue for the fiscal year, as projected by the
-
*AB5*

– 36 –
1 Economic Forum for that fiscal year pursuant to paragraph (e) of
2 subsection 1 of NRS 353.228 and as adjusted by any legislation
3 enacted by the Legislature that affects state revenue for that fiscal
4 year.
5 2. The State Board of Examiners shall consider a request
6 made pursuant to subsection 1 and shall, if it finds that a
7 suspension is warranted based on the magnitude of the shortfall in
8 revenue, recommend to the Interim Finance Committee for its
9 independent evaluation and action that the suspension be imposed
10 for a period of time not to exceed 18 months after the date on
11 which the suspension is imposed. The Interim Finance Committee
12 is not bound to follow the recommendation of the State Board of
13 Examiners.
14 3. If the Interim Finance Committee finds that a suspension
15 recommended by the State Board of Examiners should and may
16 lawfully be made, the Committee shall by resolution direct the
17 Department of Taxation and the Nevada Gaming Control Board to
18 suspend the redemption of any film infrastructure transferable tax
19 credits issued pursuant to section 11 of this act or any
20 noninfrastructure transferable tax credits issued pursuant to NRS
21 360.759, or both, for a period of time not to exceed 18 months
22 after the date on which the suspension is imposed.
23 4. If a resolution is issued pursuant to subsection 3:
24 (a) The expiration date for film infrastructure transferable tax
25 credits set forth pursuant to section 15 of this act and
26 noninfrastructure transferable tax credits set forth pursuant to
27 NRS 360.7594, for which the suspension is imposed, must be
28 extended by the number of days that such transferable tax credits
29 may not be redeemed pursuant to the resolution.
30 (b) The total amount of film infrastructure transferable tax
31 credits set forth pursuant to section 15 of this act and
32 noninfrastructure transferable tax credits set forth pursuant to
33 NRS 360.7594 used by all taxpayers must not exceed 133 percent
34 of the total amount of film infrastructure transferable tax credits
35 pursuant to section 15 of this act and noninfrastructure
36 transferable tax credits pursuant to NRS 360.7594 authorized for
37 a fiscal year beginning on or after July 1, 2029, and before
38 June 30, 2044.
39 (c) For the purposes of paragraph (b), film infrastructure
40 transferable tax credits set forth pursuant to section 15 of this act
41 and noninfrastructure transferable tax credits set forth pursuant
42 to NRS 360.7594 must be accepted based on the date on which
43 they were issued, with the credits issued earliest in time accepted
44 until the limit set forth in paragraph (b) is met.

16 (b) “Fringe benefits” means employee expenses paid by an

18 limitation, payments made to a governmental entity, union dues,

24 payments for services performed in this State by a qualified
25 individual; and

32 (1) Any natural person related to the production company

25 Sec. 34. As used in sections 34 to 40, inclusive, of this act,
26 unless the context otherwise requires, the words and terms defined

29 Sec. 35. “Account” means the Account for Nevada Film,
30 Media and Related Technology Education and Vocational
31 Training created by section 38 of this act.
32 Sec. 36. “Board” means the Board for Nevada Film, Media
33 and Related Technology Education and Vocational Training

37 Sec. 38. 1. The Account for Nevada Film, Media and
38 Related Technology Education and Vocational Training is hereby
39 created in the State General Fund. The Executive Director of the
40 Office of Economic Development, at the direction of the Board,
41 shall administer the Account.
42 2. The Executive Director may apply for and accept gifts,
43 grants, bequests and donations from any source for deposit in the
44 Account.
45 3. The Account consists of:
-
*AB5*

– 59 –
1 (a) Money transferred to the Account pursuant to NRS
2 360.759 and section 11 of this act.
3 (b) Any direct legislative appropriations to the Account.
4 (c) Any gifts, grants, bequests and donations made to the
5 Account.
6 (d) Interest and income earned on money in the Account.
7 4. The interest and income earned on the money in the
8 Account, after deducting any applicable charges, must be credited
9 to the Account.
10 5. Any money remaining in the Account at the end of the
11 fiscal year does not revert to the State General Fund, and the
12 balance in the Account must be carried forward to the next fiscal
13 year.
14 6. Money in the Account must be used by the Office to make
15 grants to any institution within the Nevada System of Higher
16 Education, a state or local agency, a school district, a charter
17 school, a vocational trade school, a nonprofit organization, a labor
18 organization or a private postsecondary educational institution
19 that provides a program of workforce development for the
20 production of qualified productions in this State. Thirty percent of
21 the money which is distributed from the Account in the form of
22 grants must be allocated to the Nevada Partners Vocational
23 Training Studio for the operation and overhead costs of the
24 Nevada Partners Vocational Training Studio. Seventy percent of
25 the money which is distributed from the Account in the form of
26 grants must be allocated to educational and vocational training
27 organizations pursuant to section 40 of this act for the purpose of
28 providing programs of workforce development for the production
29 of qualified productions in this State.
30 7. As used in this section, “qualified production” has the
31 meaning ascribed to it in NRS 360.7586.
32 Sec. 39. 1. There is hereby created the Board for Nevada
33 Film, Media and Related Technology Education and Vocational

41 (d) One member, who must not be a Legislator, appointed by

43 (e) One member, who must not be a Legislator, appointed by
44 the Minority Leader of the Assembly;
-
*AB5*

1 (f) Two members appointed by the Governor from nominees
2 selected by the lead participant in the Summerlin Production

15 subsection 1, the appointing authorities set forth in that subsection

19 (e) and (g) of subsection 1, and one member appointed pursuant to

22 appointed pursuant to paragraphs (b), (d) and (h) of subsection 1,
23 and one member appointed pursuant to paragraph (f) of
24 subsection 1, must be appointed to an initial term of 4 years
25 commencing on January 1, 2028. After the initial terms, each
26 appointed member shall serve a term of 4 years. Each appointed
27 member serves at the pleasure of the person appointing that
28 member pursuant to subsection 1. If, for any reason, a vacancy
29 occurs during the term of an appointed member, the person who is
30 responsible for making the appointment pursuant to subsection 1
31 shall appoint a replacement qualified pursuant to that subsection
32 to serve for the remainder of the unexpired term. Each appointed
33 member may serve not more than three consecutive full terms.
34 4. At the first meeting of each fiscal year, the Board shall
35 elect from among its members a Chair and a Vice Chair. The
36 Executive Director of the Office of Economic Development shall
37 serve as the nonvoting Secretary of the Board.
38 5. A majority of the voting members of the Board constitutes
39 a quorum, and the affirmative vote of a majority of the voting
40 members of the Board is required to exercise any power conferred
41 on the Board.
42 6. The Board shall meet at least twice each calendar year but
43 may meet more often at the call of the Chair or a majority of the
44 voting members of the Board.

1 7. The members of the Board serve without compensation but
2 are entitled to receive the per diem allowance and travel expenses
3 provided for state officers and employees generally while engaged
4 in the official business of the Board.
5 8. A member of the Board who is an officer or employee of
6 this State or a political subdivision of this State must be relieved
7 from duties without loss of regular compensation so that the
8 officer or employee may prepare for and attend meetings of the
9 Board and perform any work necessary to carry out the duties of
10 the Board in the most timely manner practicable. A state agency or
11 political subdivision of this State shall not require an officer or
12 employee who is a member of the Board to make up the time the

32 grant and any other information deemed necessary by the Board.
33 The Board shall provide to the Office a compilation of the
34 information provided in reports made by recipients pursuant to
35 this paragraph.
36 2. The Executive Director of the Office of Economic
37 Development may provide advice and recommendations regarding
38 the procedures, criteria and requirements established by the Board
39 pursuant to subsection 1.
40 3. The Office shall not make a grant of money from the
41 Account unless the Board has approved the application for the
42 grant.
43 Sec. 41. The provisions of subsection 1 of NRS 218D.380 do
44 not apply to any provision of this act which adds or revises a
45 requirement to submit a report to the Legislature.

1 Sec. 42. As soon as practicable after entering into a
2 development agreement that satisfies the requirements of section 10
3 of this act with the lead participant of the Summerlin Production
4 Studios Project described in section 9 of this act, the Executive

8 Sec. 43. The Office of Economic Development, the Nevada
9 Gaming Commission and the Nevada Tax Commission shall each
10 adopt such regulations as are respectively required to implement the
11 provisions of this act on or before December 31, 2026.
12 Sec. 44. The amendatory provisions of sections 21 to 33,
13 inclusive, of this act do not apply to any qualified production for
14 which an application for a certificate of eligibility for
15 noninfrastructure transferable tax credits is approved pursuant to
16 NRS 360.759 before January 1, 2027.

18 1. In preparing the Nevada Revised Statutes, use the authority
19 set forth in subsection 10 of NRS 220.120 to substitute
20 appropriately the term “noninfrastructure transferable tax credits” in
21 NRS 360.758 to 360.7598, inclusive, for the term “transferable tax
22 credits” as previously used in those sections.
23 2. In preparing supplements to the Nevada Administrative
24 Code, substitute appropriately the term “noninfrastructure
25 transferable tax credits” in NAC 360.800 to 360.865, inclusive, for
26 the term “transferable tax credits” as previously used in those
27 sections.
28 Sec. 46. If any provision of this act, or the application thereof
29 to any person, thing or circumstance is held invalid, such invalidity
30 shall not affect the provisions or application of this act which can be
31 given effect without the invalid provision or application, and to this
32 end the provisions of this act are declared to be severable.
33 Sec. 47. Notwithstanding the provisions of NRS 218D.430 and
34 218D.435, a committee may vote on this act before the expiration of
35 the period prescribed for the return of a fiscal note in NRS
36 218D.475. This section applies retroactively from and after
37 November 13, 2025.
38 Sec. 48. 1. This section becomes effective upon passage and
39 approval.
40 2. Sections 1 to 20, inclusive, and 33 to 47, inclusive, of this
41 act become effective:
42 (a) Upon passage and approval for the purpose of adopting
43 regulations and performing any other preparatory administrative
44 tasks. For the purposes of this paragraph, “preparatory
45 administrative tasks” include, without limitation, the negotiation,
